Envoy are registered at configuration time and executed at runtime through a well-defined architecture spanning multiple components:\\n\\n## Configuration Schema (Protocol Buffers)\\nThe `HttpConnectionManager` message in `envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/http_connection_manager.proto` (data-plane-api) defines the top-level configuration. It contains a `repeated HttpFilter http_filters` field (line 471) that specifies the HTTP filters to apply to all requests. Each `HttpFilter` message (lines 1339-1381) contains a `name`, an optional `typed_config` for filter-specific configuration, and flags like `is_optional` and `disabled`.\\n\\n## Configuration Processing\\nWhen Envoy starts, the `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` constructor in `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.cc` (lines 346-744) is called. This class implements the `FilterChainFactory` interface. During construction (lines 709-715), it uses the `FilterChainHelper<FactoryContext, NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory>` template class to process the `http_filters` from the protobuf config.\\n\\nThe `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` method (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h, lines 87-102) iterates through each HttpFilter in the configuration. For each filter, `FilterChainHelper::processFilter()` (lines 105-165) performs dependency validation, instantiates the appropriate filter factory based on the registered filter name, calls the factory's `createFilterFactoryFromProto()` method to create a `FilterFactoryCb` (a callback function that creates filter instances), and stores it in a list of filter factories. These factories are stored in `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::filter_factories_` for the main HTTP filter chain.\\n\\n## Upgrade Filter Chains\\nFor HTTP upgrade scenarios (like WebSocket), separate filter chains can be configured. The `HttpConnectionManager::upgrade_configs` field allows per-upgrade-type filter chains. These are processed similarly by `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` and stored in `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::upgrade_filter_factories_` as a map keyed by upgrade type (config.cc, lines 717-743).\\n\\n## Runtime Filter Chain Creation\\nAt runtime, when a new HTTP stream arrives:\\n\\n1. The `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` method (conn_manager_impl.cc, lines 378-427) is called by the underlying codec when a new request headers frame arrives.\\n\\n2. This method creates a new `ConnectionManagerImpl::ActiveStream` (lines 398-399), which instantiates a `FilterManager` object (lines 782-789). The FilterManager is passed a reference to the `FilterChainFactory` (the `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` instance) from `connection_manager_.config_->filterFactory()`.\\n\\n3. The FilterManager also receives the filter chain options and creates access log handlers from the configuration.\\n\\n4. When the first request headers are received and decoded by the HTTP codec, the stream decoding process begins. The `ActiveStream` eventually calls `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` (filter_manager.cc, lines 1550-1586).\\n\\n## Filter Chain Execution\\nThe `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` method checks if an upgrade header exists. If it does, it calls `FilterChainFactory::createUpgradeFilterChain()` (the HttpConnectionManagerConfig's override), which looks up the upgrade type in the upgrade factories and applies those filters. If no upgrade or upgrade creation fails, it calls `FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain()` (lines 1584), which is implemented in HttpConnectionManagerConfig (config.cc, lines 780-784).\\n\\nThe `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::createFilterChain()` method calls `FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()` with the stored `filter_factories_` list. This utility function iterates through each stored filter factory and calls `FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()` (filter_manager.cc, lines 551-554) for each one. This creates a `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl` object and invokes the stored `FilterFactoryCb`, which instantiates the actual filter instance and registers it with the FilterManager via callbacks like `addStreamDecoderFilter()` or `addStreamEncoderFilter()`.\\n\\nOnce the filter chain is created, as request data arrives (headers, body, trailers), the FilterManager drives data through the decoder filter chain via `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, and `decodeTrailers()` methods (filter_manager.cc, lines 569+). Each filter in the chain processes the data in order, and filters can stop iteration to perform asynchronous work before continuing. Response data flows through the encoder filter chain in reverse order.\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n- **Factory Pattern**: Filter factories are registered globally and looked up by name during configuration.\\n- **Callback Chain**: Filter factory callbacks capture filter construction logic; when invoked, they instantiate the actual filter.\\n- **Manager Pattern**: The FilterManager orchestrates data flow through the filters, maintaining iteration state and handling filter callbacks.\\n- **Configuration Providers**: Both static (configuration-time created) and dynamic (loaded via xDS) filter configurations are supported via `FilterConfigProvider` abstractions.\\n\\nThis architecture allows Envoy to support dynamic filter configuration updates (ECDS), route-based filter disabling, and complex filter dependencies while maintaining a clean separation between configuration and runtime execution.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1728,"cache_read_input_tokens":97725,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1728},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5ba3d903-9996-4a84-bb57-5a098da0bcb4","uuid":"9d10ee68-57b2-4418-9886-1d6b0a28e09e"}

`HttpConnectionManager` message in `envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/http_connection_manager.proto` (data-plane-api) defines the top-level configuration. It contains a `repeated HttpFilter http_filters` field (line 471) that specifies the HTTP filters to apply to all requests. Each `HttpFilter` message (lines 1339-1381) contains a `name`, an optional `typed_config` for filter-specific configuration, and flags like `is_optional` and `disabled`.\\n\\n## Configuration Processing\\nWhen Envoy starts, the `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` constructor in `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.cc` (lines 346-744) is called. This class implements the `FilterChainFactory` interface. During construction (lines 709-715), it uses the `FilterChainHelper<FactoryContext, NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory>` template class to process the `http_filters` from the protobuf config.\\n\\nThe `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` method (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h, lines 87-102) iterates through each HttpFilter in the configuration. For each filter, `FilterChainHelper::processFilter()` (lines 105-165) performs dependency validation, instantiates the appropriate filter factory based on the registered filter name, calls the factory's `createFilterFactoryFromProto()` method to create a `FilterFactoryCb` (a callback function that creates filter instances), and stores it in a list of filter factories. These factories are stored in `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::filter_factories_` for the main HTTP filter chain.\\n\\n## Upgrade Filter Chains\\nFor HTTP upgrade scenarios (like WebSocket), separate filter chains can be configured. The `HttpConnectionManager::upgrade_configs` field allows per-upgrade-type filter chains. These are processed similarly by `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` and stored in `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::upgrade_filter_factories_` as a map keyed by upgrade type (config.cc, lines 717-743).\\n\\n## Runtime Filter Chain Creation\\nAt runtime, when a new HTTP stream arrives:\\n\\n1. The `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` method (conn_manager_impl.cc, lines 378-427) is called by the underlying codec when a new request headers frame arrives.\\n\\n2. This method creates a new `ConnectionManagerImpl::ActiveStream` (lines 398-399), which instantiates a `FilterManager` object (lines 782-789). The FilterManager is passed a reference to the `FilterChainFactory` (the `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` instance) from `connection_manager_.config_->filterFactory()`.\\n\\n3. The FilterManager also receives the filter chain options and creates access log handlers from the configuration.\\n\\n4. When the first request headers are received and decoded by the HTTP codec, the stream decoding process begins. The `ActiveStream` eventually calls `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` (filter_manager.cc, lines 1550-1586).\\n\\n## Filter Chain Execution\\nThe `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` method checks if an upgrade header exists. If it does, it calls `FilterChainFactory::createUpgradeFilterChain()` (the HttpConnectionManagerConfig's override), which looks up the upgrade type in the upgrade factories and applies those filters. If no upgrade or upgrade creation fails, it calls `FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain()` (lines 1584), which is implemented in HttpConnectionManagerConfig (config.cc, lines 780-784).\\n\\nThe `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::createFilterChain()` method calls `FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()` with the stored `filter_factories_` list. This utility function iterates through each stored filter factory and calls `FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()` (filter_manager.cc, lines 551-554) for each one. This creates a `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl` object and invokes the stored `FilterFactoryCb`, which instantiates the actual filter instance and registers it with the FilterManager via callbacks like `addStreamDecoderFilter()` or `addStreamEncoderFilter()`.\\n\\nOnce the filter chain is created, as request data arrives (headers, body, trailers), the FilterManager drives data through the decoder filter chain via `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, and `decodeTrailers()` methods (filter_manager.cc, lines 569+). Each filter in the chain processes the data in order, and filters can stop iteration to perform asynchronous work before continuing. Response data flows through the encoder filter chain in reverse order.\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n- **Factory Pattern**: Filter factories are registered globally and looked up by name during configuration.\\n- **Callback Chain**: Filter factory callbacks capture filter construction logic; when invoked, they instantiate the actual filter.\\n- **Manager Pattern**: The FilterManager orchestrates data flow through the filters, maintaining iteration state and handling filter callbacks.\\n- **Configuration Providers**: Both static (configuration-time created) and dynamic (loaded via xDS) filter configurations are supported via `FilterConfigProvider` abstractions.\\n\\nThis architecture allows Envoy to support dynamic filter configuration updates (ECDS), route-based filter disabling, and complex filter dependencies while maintaining a clean separation between configuration and runtime execution.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Envoy are registered at configuration time and executed at runtime through a well-defined architecture spanning multiple components:\\n\\n## Configuration Schema (Protocol Buffers)\\nThe `HttpConnectionManager` message in `envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/http_connection_manager.proto` (data-plane-api) defines the top-level configuration. It contains a `repeated HttpFilter http_filters` field (line 471) that specifies the HTTP filters to apply to all requests. Each `HttpFilter` message (lines 1339-1381) contains a `name`, an optional `typed_config` for filter-specific configuration, and flags like `is_optional` and `disabled`.\\n\\n## Configuration Processing\\nWhen Envoy starts, the `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` constructor in `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.cc` (lines 346-744) is called. This class implements the `FilterChainFactory` interface. During construction (lines 709-715), it uses the `FilterChainHelper<FactoryContext, NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory>` template class to process the `http_filters` from the protobuf config.\\n\\nThe `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` method (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h, lines 87-102) iterates through each HttpFilter in the configuration. For each filter, `FilterChainHelper::processFilter()` (lines 105-165) performs dependency validation, instantiates the appropriate filter factory based on the registered filter name, calls the factory's `createFilterFactoryFromProto()` method to create a `FilterFactoryCb` (a callback function that creates filter instances), and stores it in a list of filter factories. These factories are stored in `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::filter_factories_` for the main HTTP filter chain.\\n\\n## Upgrade Filter Chains\\nFor HTTP upgrade scenarios (like WebSocket), separate filter chains can be configured. The `HttpConnectionManager::upgrade_configs` field allows per-upgrade-type filter chains. These are processed similarly by `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` and stored in `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::upgrade_filter_factories_` as a map keyed by upgrade type (config.cc, lines 717-743).\\n\\n## Runtime Filter Chain Creation\\nAt runtime, when a new HTTP stream arrives:\\n\\n1. The `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` method (conn_manager_impl.cc, lines 378-427) is called by the underlying codec when a new request headers frame arrives.\\n\\n2. This method creates a new `ConnectionManagerImpl::ActiveStream` (lines 398-399), which instantiates a `FilterManager` object (lines 782-789). The FilterManager is passed a reference to the `FilterChainFactory` (the `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` instance) from `connection_manager_.config_->filterFactory()`.\\n\\n3. The FilterManager also receives the filter chain options and creates access log handlers from the configuration.\\n\\n4. When the first request headers are received and decoded by the HTTP codec, the stream decoding process begins. The `ActiveStream` eventually calls `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` (filter_manager.cc, lines 1550-1586).\\n\\n## Filter Chain Execution\\nThe `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` method checks if an upgrade header exists. If it does, it calls `FilterChainFactory::createUpgradeFilterChain()` (the HttpConnectionManagerConfig's override), which looks up the upgrade type in the upgrade factories and applies those filters. If no upgrade or upgrade creation fails, it calls `FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain()` (lines 1584), which is implemented in HttpConnectionManagerConfig (config.cc, lines 780-784).\\n\\nThe `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::createFilterChain()` method calls `FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()` with the stored `filter_factories_` list. This utility function iterates through each stored filter factory and calls `FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()` (filter_manager.cc, lines 551-554) for each one. This creates a `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl` object and invokes the stored `FilterFactoryCb`, which instantiates the actual filter instance and registers it with the FilterManager via callbacks like `addStreamDecoderFilter()` or `addStreamEncoderFilter()`.\\n\\nOnce the filter chain is created, as request data arrives (headers, body, trailers), the FilterManager drives data through the decoder filter chain via `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, and `decodeTrailers()` methods (filter_manager.cc, lines 569+). Each filter in the chain processes the data in order, and filters can stop iteration to perform asynchronous work before continuing. Response data flows through the encoder filter chain in reverse order.\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n- **Factory Pattern**: Filter factories are registered globally and looked up by name during configuration.\\n- **Callback Chain**: Filter factory callbacks capture filter construction logic; when invoked, they instantiate the actual filter.\\n- **Manager Pattern**: The FilterManager orchestrates data flow through the filters, maintaining iteration state and handling filter callbacks.\\n- **Configuration Providers**: Both static (configuration-time created) and dynamic (loaded via xDS) filter configurations are supported via `FilterConfigProvider` abstractions.\\n\\nThis architecture allows Envoy to support dynamic filter configuration updates (ECDS), route-based filter disabling, and complex filter dependencies while maintaining a clean separation between configuration and runtime execution.\"\n}\n","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":150}}}
